 It has adopted three methods of amendment: (a) amendment by ordinary law, (b) by special majority of Parliament, (c) special majority of Parliament and amendment with the approval of the state legislatures
 1
 By ordinary law: a bill passed by a simple majority of Parliament becomes law upon the President's assent
 iske antargat raashtrapati kii purv anumati milane par nimna sanshodhan kiye ja sakate hai:(a)nae rajyon kaa nirmaan,(b)rajya kshetra, seemaa or naam main parivartan,(c)samvidhan kii naagarikta sambandhi anusuchit kshetron or janajatiyon kii prashasan sambandhi tathaa centre dwaara prashasit kshetron kii prashasan sambandhi vyavasthaaen
 2
 vishesh bahumat dwaara sanshodhan:yadi sansad ke prayek sadan dwaara kul sadasyon kaa bahumat tathaa upasthiti or matdaan main bhaag lenevaale sadasyon ke 2 / 3 maton se vidheyak paarit ho jaaen to raashtrapati kii sweekruti milte hi vah sanshodhan samvidhan kaa ang ban jaataa he
 Except for some specific things like the judiciary and the rights and powers of the states, all other arrangements of the Constitution are amended by this process
 3
 Amendment by special majority of Parliament and acceptance of State Legislatures: For amendment of certain Articles of the Constitution, the Bill requires approval by a special majority of both the Houses of Parliament and half of the total Legislatures of the States
